        <section class="block block-views clearfix" id="block-views-ti-amg-fw-blog-details-block">
         <div class="view view-ti-amg-fw-blog-details view-id-ti_amg_fw_blog_details view-display-id-block view-dom-id-0efa2c72dffe8c52c193d47d86a9461d">
          <div class="view-content">
           <div class="views-row views-row-1 views-row-odd views-row-first views-row-last">
            <div class="views-field views-field-field-topic">
             <div class="field-content">
              <div class="bubble-container">
               <div class="bubble">
                Make This Now
                <span class="pointer">
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="views-field views-field-title">
             <h1 class="field-content">
              <a class="active" href="/blogs/2014/09/21/11-foods-you-need-for-an-oktoberfest-feast">
               11 Foods You Need for an Oktoberfest Feast
              </a>
             </h1>
            </div>
            <div class="views-field views-field-published-at">
             <div class="field-content byline">
              BY
              <a href="/contributors/justine-sterling">
               Justine  Sterling
              </a>
              | POSTED September 21, 2014  AT 2:00PM EDT
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="views-field views-field-field-image">
             <div class="field-content">
              <div class="node-image blog-Left">
               <div class="Left">
                <img alt="" data-pin-media="http://cdn-image.foodandwine.com/sites/default/files/HD-201310-r-bavarian-beer-hall-pork-shanks.jpg" height="300" src="http://cdn-image.foodandwine.com/sites/default/files/styles/300x300/public/HD-201310-r-bavarian-beer-hall-pork-shanks.jpg?itok=Wjezd4uL" typeof="foaf:Image" width="300"/>
               </div>
               <div class="image-caption">
                <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/bavarian-beer-hall-pork-shanks">
                 Bavarian Beer Hall Pork Shanks
                </a>
               </div>
               <div class="image-credit">
                 Madeleine Hill
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="views-field views-field-body">
             <div class="field-content">
              <p>
               If you were in Bavaria, you wouldnt be reading this right now. Its Oktoberfest, so you would be out celebrating with lots and lots of beer and just as much food. While you cant have the full Oktoberfest experience (unless you are, in fact, in Bavariain which case, stop reading this now), you can eat like youre there. Here, 11 traditional Oktoberfest foods.
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                Roast Chicken
               </strong>
               <br/>
               During Oktoberfest, chickens are spit-roasted until the skin is golden brown and crispy. Most people dont have a rotisserie set up at home, so instead make this classic
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/lemon-thyme-roast-chicken" target="_blank">
                lemon-thyme roast chicken
               </a>
               in the oven. Rubbing a lemon-and-thyme butter over the chicken before roasting ensures superbly crispy skin.
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                <em>
                 Schweinebraten
                </em>
                (roast pork)
               </strong>
               <br/>
               A classic Bavarian dish,
               <em>
                schweinebraten
               </em>
               can be made with a variety of pork cuts, like shoulder or even loin. Its traditionally roasted with dark beer and onions. For a quick and easy take on the dish, try this pounded
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/pork-tenderloin-smothered-in-onion-and-mustard" target="_blank">
                pork tenderloin smothered in onion and mustard
               </a>
               .
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                <em>
                 Schweinshaxe
                </em>
                (roasted ham hock)
               </strong>
               <br/>
               A beloved beer hall classic, roasted ham hock or shank (pig knuckles) are crispy on the outside with tender meat. Theyre surprisingly easy to make at home. Try it with Andrew Zimmerns
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/bavarian-beer-hall-pork-shanks" target="_blank">
                delicious recipe
               </a>
               .
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                <em>
                 Steckerlfisch
                </em>
                (grilled fish on a stick)
               </strong>
               <br/>
               Simple and fairly self-explanatory,
               <em>
                steckerlfisch
               </em>
               is marinated, skewered and grilled fish typically made with local Bavarian fish, like bream, though it can also be made with trout or mackerel. At home, try
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/grilled-sardines-with-herbed-fennel-and-olive-salad" target="_blank">
                quick-grilling sardines
               </a>
               .
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                <em>
                 Wrstl
                </em>
                (sausages)
               </strong>
               <br/>
               <em>
                Wrstl
               </em>
               refers to a variety of classic Bavarian sausages. Try them at home sauted in a skillet
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/sauteed-german-sausages-with-bacon-and-apple-sauerkraut" target="_blank">
                with bacon and apple sauerkraut
               </a>
               . Serve with plenty of mustard.
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                <em>
                 Brezen
                </em>
                (pretzels)
               </strong>
               <br/>
               You cant have Oktoberfest without pretzels. Large and soft, theyre the perfect accompaniment to beer. Try making your own with this ber-authentic recipe for
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/german-style-pretzels" target="_blank">
                German-style pretzels
               </a>
               .
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                <em>
                 Kndel
                </em>
                (potato or flour dumplings)
               </strong>
               <br/>
               These are large, dense, ultra-comforting dumplings, common in Central Europe. While
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/hungarian-potato-dumplings" target="_blank">
                these potato dumplings
               </a>
               are technically Hungarian, the idea is the same. They are like rustic gnocchi.
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                <em>
                 Ksesptzle
                </em>
                (cheese noodles)
               </strong>
               <br/>
               This is a savory, cheesy version of sptzle, a traditional egg noodle.
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/fresh-cheese-spaetzle" target="_blank">
                This recipe
               </a>
               , made with small-curd cottage cheese, is topped with tangy quark, for a doubly cheesy dish.
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                <em>
                 Reiberdatschi
                </em>
                (potato pancakes)
               </strong>
               <br/>
               These potato pancakes are served both savory with a salad or sweet with apple sauce.
               <em>
                Reiberdatschi
               </em>
               are a lot like latkes, so follow Andrew Zimmerns
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/killer-potato-latkes" target="_blank">
                killer latke recipe
               </a>
               for hot and crisp results.
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                Sauerkraut
               </strong>
               <br/>
               If youre attending Oktoberfest, youre eating this pickled cabbage with almost anything.
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/homemade-sauerkraut-with-caraway-and-apples" target="_blank">
                This homemade version
               </a>
               mixes cabbage with sweet apples and aromatic caraway.
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                <em>
                 Obatzda
                </em>
                (spiced cheese-butter spread)
               </strong>
               <br/>
               This might be your new favorite spread. Its aged soft cheese, like Camembert, mixed with butter, a small amount of beer, and spices including paprika, salt, pepper and garlic. Try
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/recipes/paprika-cheese-spread" target="_blank">
                this upscale version
               </a>
               , made with crme frache and Dijon mustard along with farmers cheese and, of course, butter.
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                Related:
               </strong>
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/slideshows/roast-chicken" target="_blank">
                33 Roast Chicken Recipes
               </a>
               <br/>
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/slideshows/sausage-recipes" target="_blank">
                22 Sausage Recipes
               </a>
               <br/>
               <a href="http://www.foodandwine.com/slideshows/grilled-pork" target="_blank">
                25 Great Grilled Pork Recipes
               </a>
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
        </section>
